<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_indigenous_peoples" title="Climate change and indigenous peoples">Climate change and indigenous peoples</a></div>
<p>A WRI report mentions that "tenure-secure" Indigenous lands generates billions and sometimes trillions of dollars' worth of benefits in the form of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_sequestration" title="Carbon sequestration">carbon sequestration</a>, reduced pollution, clean water and more. It says that tenure-secure Indigenous lands have low deforestation rates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> they help to reduce GHG emissions, control erosion and flooding by anchoring soil, and provide a suite of other local, regional and global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a>.
However, many of these communities find themselves on the front lines of the deforestation crisis, and their lives and livelihoods threatened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_people_and_environment">Indigenous people and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Indigenous people and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Misconceptions about complexity of the relationship between indigenous population and their natural habitat has informed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westerners" title="Westerners">Westerners</a> view of California's "wild Eden" which may have led to misguided ideas on policy designs to preserve this "wilderness". Assuming that the natural habitat automatically provided food and nourishment for indigenous population placed practices toward the exploitative end of the spectrum of human interactions with nature as only "hunter-gatherers". There is evidence that tells another story and describes this relationship as a "calculated tempered use of nature as active agents of environmental change and stewardship". This distorted view of "wilderness" as uninhabited nature has resulted in removal of indigenous inhabitants to preserve "the wild". In reality, depriving the land from indigenous people management such as controlled burning, harvesting, and seed scattering has yielded dense understory shrubbery or tickets of young trees which are inhospitable to life. Current assessments indicate that indigenous peoples used land sustainably, without causing substantial losses of biodiversity, for thousands of years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>A goal is to ascertain an unbiased view of indigenous population resource management practices instead of literature that often assumes their impact to be entirely negative or of little to no effect. Although, there is evidence of negative impacts, particularly, on large animals by over-exploitation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> there is a plethora of evidence from historical literature, archaeological findings, ecological field studies, and native people's culture that paints another picture in which indigenous land management practices were largely successful in promoting habitat heterogeneity, increasing <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, and maintaining certain vegetation types. These findings show that indigenous practices sustain lives while conserving natural resources and may be prove essential in improving our own relationship with natural resources. Setting aside "wilderness" is still imperative given our continued population growth, however, that growth itself requires another way of thinking in "re-creating specific human-ecosystem associations". Human-ecological history of land should inform resource management policies today. This history cannot be simplified into dichotomies of "hunter-gatherers" vs. "agriculturalists" and should entail more complex models. Indigenous practices are at the roots of this history, present a prime example of this complex relationship, and show how weaving their way of life into our culture allows us to meet our needs without destroying natural resources. It is really important that studying <a href="/wiki/Ethnoscience" title="Ethnoscience">ethnoscience</a> is not guarantee that every local societies and indigenous people must have special science to consider importan<small>t.</small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contradictory_findings">Contradictory findings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Contradictory findings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Recently, it has come to light that the <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> rate of Indonesian rainforests has been far greater than estimated. Such a rate could not have been the product of <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> as understood before; rather, it seemed that ordinary local people dependent on these forests for their livelihoods are in fact "joining distant corporations in creating uninhabitable landscapes." Popular theories of globalization cannot accommodate such phenomena. These conventions "package all cultural development into a single program" and assert that powerless minorities and communities have adjusted themselves according to global forces. However, in the case of Indonesian deforestation, global forces alone could not explain the rate of destruction. Therefore, a new approach is in which global forces are themselves "congeries of local/global interaction" with unexpected encounters across different populations and cultures. Then, destruction of forests in excess of market needs could be seen as an unexpected result of the encounter between global forces that feed the market needs and local livelihoods that depend on the same forests.  Trying to capture these unexpected encounters under the idea of "friction" where culture is "continually co-produced in interactions" that are made up of "creative qualities of interconnection across difference" might seem awkward, unequal, or unstable. These "messy and surprising" features of such interactions across difference are exactly what should inform our models of cultural production. In this framework, friction makes global connection powerful and effective but at the same time, it has the capacity to disrupt and even cause cataclysms in its smooth operation as a well-oiled machine. A well-documented example of such process is the industrialization of rubber, which was made possible by European savage conquests, competitive passions of colonial botany, resistance strategies of peasants, wars, advancement of technology and science, and the struggle over industrial goals and hierarchies. Attention to friction provides a unique opportunity to create a theoretical framework under which developing an "ethnographic" account of globalization becomes a possibility. Within such an ethnographic account, Indonesian encounters can "shape the shared space in which Indonesian and non-Indonesian jointly experience fears, tensions, and uncertainties."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studying indigenous knowledge and their relationship with nature does not make it obligatory for indigenous people to have local knowledge to consider their rights.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup"><span title="The sentence is ungrammatical and its meaning isn't clear (February 2022)">incomprehensible</span></a></i>]</sup> Criticizing environmentalist accounts of indigenous populations that are typically motivated by trying to protect their landscape and surroundings from globalization forces might be a good idea. To do so requires a two-fold strategy where description of an indigenous society and their habitat must make a "narratable" story, and be of some "value" to westerners so that it can generate international support for preserving their culture and environment. Using Eastern Penan populations to demonstrate how environmentalists transform Penan's indigenous "knowledge" of their forest by pulling from ethnographies of other forest population, e.g., in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_forests" title="Amazon forests">Amazon forests</a>. In doing so, they corrupt the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_diversity" title="Cultural diversity">cultural diversity</a> of indigenous by framing them into a single narrative in the name of preserving the <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> of their habitat. In case of Easter Penan, three categories of misrepresentation is noticeable:The Molong concept is purely a stewardship notion of resource management. communities or individuals take ownership of specific trees and harvest them in such a way that allows them to exploit long-term. This notion has gained an <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Etherealism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Etherealism (page does not exist)">etherealism</a> in environmentalist writings according to western romantic notions of indigenous to tell a more connecting story. Landscape features and particularly their names in local languages provided geographical and historical information for Penan people; whereas in environmentalist accounts, it has turned into a spiritual practice where trees and rivers represent forest spirits that are sacred to the Penan people. A typical stereotype of some environmentalists' approach to ecological <a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">ethnography</a> is to present indigenous "knowledge" of nature as "valuable" to the outside world because of its hidden medicinal benefits. In reality, eastern Penan populations do not identify a medicinal stream of "knowledge". These misrepresentations in the "narrative" of indigeneity and "value" of indigenous knowledge might have been helpful for Penan's people in their struggle to protect their environment, but it might also have disastrous consequences. What happens if another case did not fit in this romantic narrative, or another indigenous knowledge did not seem beneficial to the outside world. These people were being uprooted in the first place because their communities did not fit well with the state's system of values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_peoples_by_region">Indigenous peoples by region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Indigenous peoples by region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_indigenous_peoples" title="List of indigenous peoples">List of indigenous peoples</a></div>
<p>Indigenous populations are distributed in regions throughout the globe. The numbers, condition and experience of Indigenous groups may vary widely within a given region. A comprehensive survey is further complicated by sometimes contentious membership and identification.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Africa" title="Indigenous peoples of Africa">Indigenous peoples of Africa</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Indigenous_peoples_of_Africa" title="Category:Indigenous peoples of Africa">Category:Indigenous peoples of Africa</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BushmenSan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="634" data-file-width="968" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BushmenSan.jpg/220px-BushmenSan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BushmenSan.jpg/330px-BushmenSan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BushmenSan.jpg/440px-BushmenSan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BushmenSan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Starting fire by hand, <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San people</a> in Botswana.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pygm%C3%A9es_(RDC).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="663" data-file-width="1042" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Pygm%C3%A9es_%28RDC%29.jpg/220px-Pygm%C3%A9es_%28RDC%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Pygm%C3%A9es_%28RDC%29.jpg/330px-Pygm%C3%A9es_%28RDC%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Pygm%C3%A9es_%28RDC%29.jpg/440px-Pygm%C3%A9es_%28RDC%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pygm%C3%A9es_(RDC).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/African_Pygmies" title="African Pygmies">African Pygmies</a> in Congo</div></div></div>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-colonialism" title="Post-colonialism">post-colonial</a> period, the concept of specific Indigenous peoples within the African continent has gained wider acceptance, although not without controversy. The highly diverse and numerous ethnic groups that comprise most modern, independent African states contain within them various peoples whose situation, cultures and <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> lifestyles are generally marginalized and set apart from the dominant political and economic structures of the nation. Since the late 20th century these peoples have increasingly sought recognition of their rights as distinct Indigenous peoples, in both national and international contexts.
</p><p>Though the vast majority of African peoples are indigenous in the sense that they originate from that continent, in practice, identity as an <i>Indigenous people</i> per the modern definition is more restrictive, and certainly not every African ethnic group claims identification under these terms. Groups and communities who do claim this recognition are those who, by a variety of historical and environmental circumstances, have been placed outside of the dominant state systems, and whose traditional practices and land claims often come into conflict with the objectives and policies implemented by governments, companies and surrounding dominant societies.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indigenous peoples of the Americas</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Category:Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Category:Indigenous peoples of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3194" data-file-width="4758" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg/220px-Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg/330px-Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg/440px-Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qamutik_1_1999-04-01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> on a traditional <i>qamutik</i> (dog sled) in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Dorset" title="Cape Dorset">Cape Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a>, Canada.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="1826" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg/170px-Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg/255px-Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg/340px-Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tocado_tradicional_nahua.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A girl wears the traditional <a href="/wiki/Nahuas" title="Nahuas">Nahua</a> headdress in <a href="/wiki/Yohualichan" title="Yohualichan">Yohualichan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Indigenous peoples of the Americas are broadly recognized as being those groups and their descendants who inhabited the region before the arrival of European colonizers and settlers (i.e., <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">Pre-Columbian</a>). Indigenous peoples who maintain, or seek to maintain, traditional ways of life are found from the high Arctic north to the southern extremities of <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a>.
</p><p>The impacts of historical and ongoing <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a> on Indigenous communities have been in general quite severe, with many authorities estimating ranges of significant <a href="/wiki/Population_history_of_Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Population history of Indigenous peoples of the Americas">population decline</a> primarily due to disease, land theft and violence. Several peoples have become extinct, or very nearly so. But there are and have been many thriving and resilient Indigenous nations and communities.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>North America is sometimes referred to by Indigenous peoples as <a href="/wiki/Abya_Yala" title="Abya Yala">Abya Yala</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turtle_Island_(North_America)" title="Turtle Island (North America)">Turtle Island</a>.
</p><p>In Mexico, about 25 million people self-reported as Indigenous in 2015. Some estimates put the Indigenous population of Mexico as high as 40-65 million people, making it the country with the highest Indigenous population in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In the southern states of <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a> (65.73%) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_(state)" title="Yucatán (state)">Yucatán</a> (65.40%), the majority of the population is Indigenous, as reported in 2015. Other states with high populations of Indigenous peoples include <a href="/wiki/Campeche" title="Campeche">Campeche</a> (44.54%), <a href="/wiki/Quintana_Roo" title="Quintana Roo">Quintana Roo</a>, (44.44%), <a href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(state)" title="Hidalgo (state)">Hidalgo</a>, (36.21%), <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a> (36.15%), <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a> (35.28%), and <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a> (33.92%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-somosprimos.com_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-somosprimos.com-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Canada" title="Indigenous peoples in Canada">Indigenous peoples in Canada</a> comprise the <a href="/wiki/First_Nations_in_Canada" title="First Nations in Canada">First Nations</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-First_Nations_Culture_Areas_Index_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-First_Nations_Culture_Areas_Index-61">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICCcharter_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICCcharter-62">[62]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis_people_(Canada)" title="Métis people (Canada)">Métis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>  The descriptors "Indian" and "<a href="/wiki/Eskimo" title="Eskimo">Eskimo</a>" have fallen into disuse in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indian_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Indian-65">[65]</a></sup> More currently, the term "Aboriginal" is being replaced with "Indigenous". Several national organizations in Canada changed their names from "Aboriginal" to "Indigenous". Most notable was the change of Aboriginal Affairs and Northern Development Canada (AANDC) to Indigenous and Northern Affairs Canada (INAC) in 2015, which then split into Indigenous Services Canada and Crown-Indigenous Relations and Northern Development Canada in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> According to the 2016 Census, there are around 1,670,000 Indigenous peoples in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> There are currently over 600 recognized <a href="/wiki/List_of_First_Nations_peoples" title="List of First Nations peoples">First Nations governments or bands</a> spread across Canada, such as the Cree, Mohawk, Mikmaq, Blackfoot, Coast Salish, Innu, Dene and more, with distinctive Indigenous cultures, languages, art, and music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-one_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-one-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-three_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-three-69">[69]</a></sup> First Nations peoples signed 11 numbered <a class="external text" href="https://www.thecanadianencyclopedia.ca/en/article/aboriginal-treaties" rel="nofollow">treaties</a> across much of what is now known as Canada between 1871 and 1921, except in parts of British Columbia.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> have achieved a degree of administrative autonomy with the creation in 1999 of the territories of <a href="/wiki/Nunavik" title="Nunavik">Nunavik</a> (in Northern Quebec), <a href="/wiki/Nunatsiavut" title="Nunatsiavut">Nunatsiavut</a> (in Northern Labrador) and <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a>, which was until 1999 a part of the Northwest Territories. The autonomous territory of <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a> is also home to a recognised Indigenous and majority population of Inuit (about 85%) who settled the area in the 13th century, displacing the Indigenous European <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_Norse" title="Greenlandic Norse">Greenlandic Norse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, the combined populations of Native Americans, Inuit and other Indigenous designations totaled 2,786,652 (constituting about 1.5% of 2003 U.S. census figures). Some 563 scheduled tribes are recognized at the federal level, and a number of others recognized at the state level.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_and_South_America">Central and South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Central and South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quechuawomanandchild.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Quechuawomanandchild.jpg/220px-Quechuawomanandchild.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Quechuawomanandchild.jpg/330px-Quechuawomanandchild.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Quechuawomanandchild.jpg/440px-Quechuawomanandchild.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quechuawomanandchild.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechuas" title="Quechuas">Quechua</a> woman and child in the <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Valley" title="Sacred Valley">Sacred Valley</a>, Andes, Peru</div></div></div><p>In some countries (particularly in Latin America), Indigenous peoples form a sizable component of the overall national population — in Bolivia, they account for an estimated 56–70% of the total nation, and at least half of the population in Guatemala and the Andean and Amazonian nations of Peru. In English, Indigenous peoples are collectively referred to by different names that vary by region, age and ethnicity of speakers, with <a href="/wiki/Native_American_name_controversy" title="Native American name controversy">no one term being universally accepted</a>. While still in use in-group, and in many names of organizations, "Indian" is less popular among younger people, who tend to prefer "Indigenous" or simply "<a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native</a>, with most preferring to use the specific name of their tribe or Nation instead of generalities. In Spanish or Portuguese speaking countries, one finds the use of terms such as índios, <i>pueblos <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ind%C3%ADgena" title="wikt:indígena">indígenas</a></i>, <i>amerindios</i>, <i>povos nativos</i>, <i>povos indígenas</i>, and, in Peru, <i>Comunidades Nativas</i> (Native Communities), particularly among Amazonian societies like the <a href="/wiki/Urarina" title="Urarina">Urarina</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mats%C3%A9s" title="Matsés">Matsés</a>. In Chile, there the most populous indigenous peoples are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mapuches" title="Mapuches">Mapuches</a> in the Center-South and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aymaras" title="Aymaras">Aymaras</a> in the North.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_people" title="Rapa Nui people">Rapa Nui</a> of <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a>, who are a <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesian</a> people, are the only non-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindian" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> indigenous people in Chile.
</p><p>Indigenous peoples make up 0.4% of all Brazilian population, or about 700,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Indigenous peoples are found in the entire territory of Brazil, although the majority of them live in Indian reservations in the North and Center-Western part of the country. On 18 January 2007, <a href="/wiki/Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Nacional_do_%C3%8Dndio" title="Fundação Nacional do Índio">FUNAI</a> reported that it had confirmed the presence of 67 different <a href="/wiki/Uncontacted_peoples" title="Uncontacted peoples">uncontacted peoples</a> in Brazil, up from 40 in 2005. With this addition Brazil has now overtaken the island of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> as the country having the largest number of uncontacted peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Asia" title="Indigenous peoples of Asia">Indigenous peoples of Asia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Indigenous_peoples_of_Asia" title="Category:Indigenous peoples of Asia">Category:Indigenous peoples of Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kalasha_Girls.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1875" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Kalasha_Girls.jpg/220px-Kalasha_Girls.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Kalasha_Girls.jpg/330px-Kalasha_Girls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Kalasha_Girls.jpg/440px-Kalasha_Girls.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kalasha_Girls.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kalash_people" title="Kalash people">Kalash</a> girls in Pakistan</div></div></div>
<p>The vast regions of Asia contain the majority of the world's present-day indigenous populations, about 70% according to IWGIA figures.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Asia">Western Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Western Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>: are the Indigenous people of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_Highlands" title="Armenian Highlands">Armenian Highlands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Travis_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Travis-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> There are currently more Armenians living outside their ancestral homeland because of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian genocide</a> of 1915.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anatolian_Greeks" title="Anatolian Greeks">Anatolian Greeks</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Pontic_Greeks" title="Pontic Greeks">Pontic Greeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cappadocian_Greeks" title="Cappadocian Greeks">Cappadocian Greeks</a>, are the Greek-speaking minorities that existed in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> millennia before Turkic conquest. They are indigenous to Asiatic Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Travis_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Travis-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Most were either killed in the <a href="/wiki/Greek_genocide" title="Greek genocide">Greek genocide</a> or displaced during the following <a href="/wiki/Population_exchange_between_Greece_and_Turkey" title="Population exchange between Greece and Turkey">population exchange</a>; however, some remain in Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> There has been a Greek presence in Anatolia since at least the 1000s BCE,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and Greek traders visited western Anatolia beginning in 1900 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>: are indigenous to Mesopotamia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Travis_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-Travis-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> They claim descent from the ancient <a href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire">Neo-Assyrian Empire</a>, and lived in what was <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyria</a>, their original homeland, and still speak dialects of Aramaic, the official language of the Assyrian Empire.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a>: are indigenous to <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>: are one of the Indigenous peoples of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">Yazidis</a>: are indigenous to <a href="/wiki/Upper_Mesopotamia" title="Upper Mesopotamia">Upper Mesopotamia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Travis_78-3"><a href="#cite_note-Travis-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>There are competing claims that <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinian Arabs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> are indigenous to <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">historic Palestine</a>/the <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">Land of Israel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The argument entered the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a> in the 1990s, with Palestinians claiming Indigenous status as a pre-existing population displaced by Jews,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> whom some regard as Europeans who only began to <a href="/wiki/Aliyah" title="Aliyah">immigrate to Palestine in the 19th century</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-105">[105]</a></sup> Israeli Jews have also claimed indigeneity, citing <a href="/wiki/Promised_Land" title="Promised Land">religious</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Israel_and_Judah" title="History of ancient Israel and Judah">historical connections</a> to the land as their ancient homeland; some have disputed the authenticity of Palestinian claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Negev_Bedouin" title="Negev Bedouin">Negev Bedouin</a> were officially recognised as Indigenous peoples of Israel by the United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> This has been criticised both by scholars associated with the Israeli state, who dispute the Bedouin's claim to indigeneity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> and those who argue that recognising just one group of Palestinians as indigenous risks undermining others' claims and "fetishising" nomadic cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia">South Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: South Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg/220px-Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg/330px-Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg/440px-Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sumi_dancer_girls.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Naga_people" title="Naga people">Naga people</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northeast_India" title="Northeast India">Northeast India</a></div></div></div>
<p>India's Andaman and Nicobar Islands in the Indian Ocean are also home to several Indigenous groups such as the Andamanese of Strait Island, the Jarawas of Middle Andaman and South Andaman Islands, the Onge of Little Anadaman Island and the uncontacted Sentinelese of North Sentinel Island. They are registered and protected by the Indian government.
</p><p>In Sri Lanka, the Indigenous <a href="/wiki/Vedda" title="Vedda">Vedda</a> people constitute a small minority of the population today.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Asia">North Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: North Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2998" data-file-width="2485" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg/170px-Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg/255px-Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg/340px-Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nivkh_Marina_Temina_%C3%81rran-konfer%C3%A1nssas_2019_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marina A. Temina, a native speaker and teacher of the <a href="/wiki/Nivkh_languages" title="Nivkh languages">Nivkh language</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Russians <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Siberia" title="Russian conquest of Siberia">invaded Siberia and conquered the indigenous people</a> in the 17th–18th centuries.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nivkh_people" title="Nivkh people">Nivkh people</a> are an ethnic group indigenous to <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>, having a few speakers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nivkh_language" title="Nivkh language">Nivkh language</a>, but their fisher culture has been endangered due to the development of oil field of Sakhalin from 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, definition of "indigenous peoples" is contested largely referring to a number of population (less than 50,000 people), and neglecting self-identification, origin from indigenous populations who inhabited the country or region upon invasion, colonization or establishment of state frontiers, distinctive social, economic and cultural institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7">[7]</a></sup> Thus, indigenous peoples of Russia such as Sakha, Komi, Karelian and others are not considered as such due to the size of the population (more than 50,000 people), and consequently they "are not the subjects of the specific legal protections."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The Russian government recognizes only 40 ethnic groups as indigenous peoples, even though there are other 30 groups to be counted as such. The reason of nonrecognition is the size of the population and relatively late advent to their current regions, thus indigenous peoples in Russia should be numbered less than 50,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Asia">East Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: East Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ainu_man.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3439" data-file-width="2293" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ainu_man.jpg/170px-Ainu_man.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ainu_man.jpg/255px-Ainu_man.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ainu_man.jpg/340px-Ainu_man.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ainu_man.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ainu_people" title="Ainu people">Ainu</a> man performing a traditional Ainu dance</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ainu_people" title="Ainu people">Ainu people</a> are an ethnic group indigenous to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hokkaid%C5%8D" title="Hokkaidō">Hokkaidō</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>, and much of Sakhalin. As Japanese settlement expanded, the Ainu were pushed northward and fought against the Japanese in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shakushain%27s_Revolt" title="Shakushain's Revolt">Shakushain's Revolt</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Menashi-Kunashir_Rebellion" title="Menashi-Kunashir Rebellion">Menashi-Kunashir Rebellion</a>, until by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meiji_period" title="Meiji period">Meiji period</a> they were confined by the government to a small area in Hokkaidō, in a manner similar to the placing of Native Americans on reservations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> In a ground-breaking 1997 decision involving the <a href="/wiki/Ainu_people#Litigation" title="Ainu people">Ainu people</a> of Japan, the Japanese courts recognized their claim in law, stating that "If one minority group lived in an area prior to being ruled over by a majority group and preserved its distinct ethnic culture even after being ruled over by the majority group, while another came to live in an area ruled over by a majority after consenting to the majority rule, it must be recognized that it is only natural that the distinct ethnic culture of the former group requires greater consideration."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_people" title="Dzungar people">Dzungar Oirats</a> are indigenous to the <a href="/wiki/Dzungaria" title="Dzungaria">Dzungaria</a> in Northern <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tajiks_in_China" title="Tajiks in China">Sarikoli Pamiris</a> are indigenous to <a href="/wiki/Taxkorgan_Tajik_Autonomous_County" title="Taxkorgan Tajik Autonomous County">Tashkurgan</a> in Xinjiang.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetans" title="Tibetans">Tibetans</a> are indigenous to Tibet.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ryukyuan_people" title="Ryukyuan people">Ryukyuan people</a> are indigenous to the <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands" title="Ryukyu Islands">Ryukyu Islands</a>.
</p><p>The languages of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwanese_aborigines" title="Taiwanese aborigines">Taiwanese aborigines</a> have significance in <a href="/wiki/Historical_linguistics" title="Historical linguistics">historical linguistics</a>, since in all likelihood Taiwan was the place of origin of the entire <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_language" title="Austronesian language">Austronesian language</a> family, which spread across Oceania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_inhabitants_of_the_New_Territories" title="Indigenous inhabitants of the New Territories">indigenous inhabitants of the New Territories</a> are defined in the <a href="/wiki/Sino-British_Joint_Declaration" title="Sino-British Joint Declaration">Sino-British Joint Declaration</a> as people <a href="/wiki/Patrilineality" title="Patrilineality">descended through the male line</a> from a person who was in 1898, before <a href="/wiki/Convention_for_the_Extension_of_Hong_Kong_Territory" title="Convention for the Extension of Hong Kong Territory">Convention for the Extension of Hong Kong Territory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> There are several different groups that make up the indigenous inhabitants, the <a href="/wiki/Punti" title="Punti">Punti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hakka_people" title="Hakka people">Hakka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoklo_people" title="Hoklo people">Hoklo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tanka_people" title="Tanka people">Tanka</a>. All are nonetheless considered part of the <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a> majority, although some like the Tanka have been shown to have genetic and anthropological roots in the <a href="/wiki/Baiyue" title="Baiyue">Baiyue</a> people, the pre-Han Chinese inhabitants of Southern China.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Southeast Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dayak_Parade.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Dayak_Parade.jpg/220px-Dayak_Parade.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Dayak_Parade.jpg/330px-Dayak_Parade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Dayak_Parade.jpg/440px-Dayak_Parade.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dayak_Parade.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak people</a> in Kalimantan</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Malay_Singaporeans" title="Malay Singaporeans">Malay Singaporeans</a> are the indigenous people of Singapore, inhabiting it since the Austronesian migration. They had established the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Singapura" title="Kingdom of Singapura">Kingdom of Singapura</a> back in the 13th century. The name Singapore itself comes from the Malay word Singapura (Singa=Lion, Pura=City) which means the Lion City.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Chams" title="Chams">Cham</a> are the indigenous people of the former state of <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">Champa</a> which was conquered by Vietnam in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Cham%E2%80%93Vietnamese_wars" title="History of the Cham–Vietnamese wars">Cham–Vietnamese wars</a> during <a href="/wiki/Nam_ti%E1%BA%BFn" title="Nam tiến">Nam tiến</a>. The Cham in Vietnam are only recognized as a minority, and not as an indigenous people by the Vietnamese government despite being indigenous to the region.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Degar" title="Degar">Degar</a> (Montagnards) are indigenous to <a href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_(Vietnam)" title="Central Highlands (Vietnam)">Central Highlands (Vietnam)</a> and were conquered by the Vietnamese in the <a href="/wiki/Nam_ti%E1%BA%BFn" title="Nam tiến">Nam tiến</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Krom" title="Khmer Krom">Khmer Krom</a> are the indigenous people of the <a href="/wiki/Mekong_Delta" title="Mekong Delta">Mekong Delta</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saigon" title="Saigon">Saigon</a> which were acquired by Vietnam from Cambodian King <a href="/wiki/Chey_Chettha_II" title="Chey Chettha II">Chey Chettha II</a> in exchange for a Vietnamese princess.
</p><p>In Indonesia, there are 50 to 70 million people who classify as indigenous peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> However, the Indonesian government does not recognize the existence of indigenous peoples, classifying every <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_Indonesian" title="Native Indonesian">Native Indonesian</a> ethnic group as "indigenous" despite the clear cultural distinctions of certain groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> This problem is shared by many other countries in the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> region.
</p><p>In the Philippines, there are 135 ethno-linguistic groups, majority of which are considered as indigenous peoples by mainstream indigenous ethnic groups in the country. The indigenous people of <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Administrative_Region" title="Cordillera Administrative Region">Cordillera Administrative Region</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cagayan_Valley" title="Cagayan Valley">Cagayan Valley</a> in the Philippines are the <a href="/wiki/Igorot_people" title="Igorot people">Igorot people</a>. The indigenous peoples of <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a> are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lumad_peoples" title="Lumad peoples">Lumad peoples</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Moro_people" title="Moro people">Moro</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tausug_people" title="Tausug people">Tausug</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maguindanao_people" title="Maguindanao people">Maguindanao</a> <a href="/wiki/Maranao_people" title="Maranao people">Maranao</a> and others) who also live in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sulu_archipelago" title="Sulu archipelago">Sulu archipelago</a>. There are also others sets of indigenous peoples in <a href="/wiki/Palawan" title="Palawan">Palawan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mindoro" title="Mindoro">Mindoro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a>, and the rest central and south <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>. The country has one of the largest indigenous peoples population in the world.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, indigenous peoples include the Shan, the Karen, the Rakhine, the Karenni, the Chin, the Kachin and the Mon. However, there are more ethnic groups that are considered indigenous, for example, the Akha, the Lisu, the Lahu or the Mru, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Ethnic groups in Europe</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Genetic_history_of_Europe" title="Genetic history of Europe">Genetic history of Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Indigenous_peoples_of_Europe" title="Category:Indigenous peoples of Europe">Category:Indigenous peoples of Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2170" data-file-width="1904" decoding="async" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg/170px-Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg/255px-Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg/340px-Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sami_family_Finland_1936.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A1mi_people" title="Sámi people">Sámi family</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lapland_(Finland)" title="Lapland (Finland)">Lapland</a>, 1936</div></div></div>
<p>Various <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">ethnic groups</a> have <a href="/wiki/Genetic_history_of_Europe" title="Genetic history of Europe">lived in Europe for millennia</a>. However, the UN recognizes very few indigenous populations within Europe, which are confined to the far north and far east of the continent.
</p><p>Notable indigenous minority populations in Europe that are recognized by the UN include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A1mi_people" title="Sámi people">Sámi</a> peoples of northern <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> and northwestern Russia (in an area also referred to as <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A1pmi" title="Sápmi">Sápmi</a>); the Uralic <a href="/wiki/Nenets_people" title="Nenets people">Nenets</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samoyedic_peoples" title="Samoyedic peoples">Samoyed</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Komi_peoples" title="Komi peoples">Komi</a> peoples of northern Russia;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a> of southern Russia and the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krymchaks" title="Krymchaks">Krymchaks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Karaites" title="Crimean Karaites">Crimean Karaites</a> of Crimea in Ukraine; the <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basques</a> of <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Sorbs" title="Sorbs">Sorbs</a> of Germany and Poland, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_People" title="Irish People">Irish</a> of the island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Balkans" title="The Balkans">the Balkans</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Oceania" title="Indigenous peoples of Oceania">Indigenous peoples of Oceania</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Indigenous_peoples_of_Oceania" title="Category:Indigenous peoples of Oceania">Category:Indigenous peoples of Oceania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg/240px-1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg/360px-1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg/480px-1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1981_event_Australian_aboriginals.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">Aboriginal Australian</a> dancers</div></div></div>
<p>In Australia, the indigenous populations are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australian" title="Aboriginal Australian">Aboriginal Australian</a> peoples (comprising many different nations and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australian_languages" title="Aboriginal Australian languages">language groups</a>) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torres_Strait_Islander" title="Torres Strait Islander">Torres Strait Islander</a> peoples (also with sub-groups). These two groups are often referred to as <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous Australians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> although terms such as First Nations<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and First Peoples are also used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Micronesians" title="Micronesians">Micronesian</a> peoples originally populated many of the present-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Island" title="Pacific Island">Pacific Island</a> countries in the <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> region over the course of thousands of years. European, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_colonialism" title="American colonialism">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Easter_Island" title="History of Easter Island">Chilean</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_colonies" title="Japanese colonies">Japanese</a> colonial expansion in the Pacific brought many of these areas under non-indigenous administration, mainly during the 19th century. During the 20th century, several of these former colonies gained independence and nation-states formed under local control. However, various peoples have put forward claims for indigenous recognition where their islands are still under external administration; examples include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chamorros" title="Chamorros">Chamorros</a> of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Marianas" title="Northern Marianas">Northern Marianas</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marshallese_people" title="Marshallese people">Marshallese</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>. Some islands remain under administration from Paris, Washington, London or <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Papua_20160808_0449.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Papua_20160808_0449.jpg/220px-Papua_20160808_0449.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Papua_20160808_0449.jpg/330px-Papua_20160808_0449.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Papua_20160808_0449.jpg/440px-Papua_20160808_0449.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Papua_20160808_0449.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dani_people" title="Dani people">Dani people</a> from the central highlands of <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">western New Guinea</a></div></div></div>
<p>The remains of at least 25 miniature humans, who lived between 1,000 and 3,000 years ago, were recently found on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> in Micronesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>In most parts of Oceania, indigenous peoples outnumber the descendants of colonists. Exceptions include Australia, New Zealand and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. In New Zealand the <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_people" title="Māori people">Māori</a> population estimate at 30 June 2021 is 17% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Māori are indigenous to Polynesia and settled New Zealand after migrations probably in the 13th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> A treaty with the British, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Waitangi" title="Treaty of Waitangi">Treaty of Waitangi</a> was signed in 1840 by approximately 45 Māori leaders,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> following in 1835 the signing of <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Independence_of_New_Zealand" title="Declaration of the Independence of New Zealand">He Whakaputanga o te Rangatiratanga o Nu Tirene: the Declaration of Independence of the United Tribes of New Zealand</a> as a statement of sovereignty by Māori to the wider world and an assertion of the Indigenous rights of Māori in New Zealand, this led to the Treaty of Waitangi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>A majority of the <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> population is indigenous, with more than 700 different nationalities recognized in a total population of 8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The country's constitution and key statutes identify traditional or custom-based practices and land tenure, and explicitly set out to promote the viability of these traditional societies within the modern state. However, conflicts and disputes concerning land use and resource rights continue between indigenous groups, the government, and corporate entities.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_rights_and_other_issues">Indigenous rights and other issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indigenous_peoples&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Indigenous rights and other issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
